<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Delta Goodrem</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<p><b>Delta Lea Goodrem</b> (born 9 November 1984) is an Australian singer-songwriter and actress. Born and raised in <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_South_Wales_(Australia)" title="New South Wales (Australia)">New South Wales</a>, she enrolled in dancing, acting, singing and piano classes at a young age. She began her career as a child actress, starring in various television shows and rose to prominence in 2002 in the Australian soap opera <i><a href="/wiki/Neighbours" title="Neighbours">Neighbours</a></i> as <a href="/wiki/Nina_Tucker" title="Nina Tucker">Nina Tucker</a>.</p>
<p>Venturing into the music industry, Goodrem signed to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sony_Music_Entertainment" title="Sony Music Entertainment">Sony Music</a> at the age of 15 and released her debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Innocent_Eyes_(Delta_Goodrem_album)" title="Innocent Eyes (Delta Goodrem album)">Innocent Eyes</a></i> (2003), which topped the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ARIA_Albums_Chart" title="ARIA Albums Chart">ARIA Albums Chart</a> for an all-time record of 29 consecutive weeks and reached number two on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a>. It became one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_albums_in_Australia" title="List of best-selling albums in Australia">highest-selling albums in Australian history</a>, with over four million copies sold worldwide and all five of its singles—"<a href="/wiki/Born_to_Try" title="Born to Try">Born to Try</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Lost_Without_You" title="Lost Without You">Lost Without You</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Innocent_Eyes_(song)" title="Innocent Eyes (song)">Innocent Eyes</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Not_Me,_Not_I" title="Not Me, Not I">Not Me, Not I</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Predictable_(Delta_Goodrem_song)" title="Predictable (Delta Goodrem song)">Predictable</a>—reaching number one on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ARIA_Singles_Chart" title="ARIA Singles Chart">ARIA Singles Chart</a> and the first three reaching the top ten in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK_Single_Chart" title="UK Single Chart">UK Single Chart</a>. This made Goodrem the first and only artist to have five number-one singles from a debut album. <i>Innocent Eyes</i> is the best-selling album of the 2000s decade in Australia and the debut album with the most number-one singles.</p>
<p>Her second studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Mistaken_Identity_(Delta_Goodrem_album)" title="Mistaken Identity (Delta Goodrem album)">Mistaken Identity</a></i> (2004), was created while she was suffering from cancer and several of its themes reflect this. It became her second number-one album and brought her two more number-one singles, including "<a href="/wiki/Out_of_the_Blue_(Delta_Goodrem_song)" title="Out of the Blue (Delta Goodrem song)">Out of the Blue</a>". In 2007, Goodrem released <i><a href="/wiki/Delta_(Delta_Goodrem_album)" title="Delta (Delta Goodrem album)">Delta</a></i>, her third number-one album, which saw another number-one single, "<a href="/wiki/In_This_Life_(Delta_Goodrem_song)" title="In This Life (Delta Goodrem song)">In This Life</a>". Her fourth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Child_of_the_Universe_(album)" title="Child of the Universe (album)">Child of the Universe</a></i> (2012), produced the successful single "<a href="/wiki/Sitting_on_Top_of_the_World_(Delta_Goodrem_song)" title="Sitting on Top of the World (Delta Goodrem song)">Sitting on Top of the World</a>". In 2016, her fifth album, <i><a href="/wiki/Wings_of_the_Wild" title="Wings of the Wild">Wings of the Wild</a></i>, became her fourth number-one album on the ARIA Albums Chart, while giving her another number-one single, "<a href="/wiki/Wings_(Delta_Goodrem_song)" title="Wings (Delta Goodrem song)">Wings</a>".</p>
<p>Goodrem has a total of nine number-one singles and 17 top-ten hits on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ARIA_Singles_Chart" title="ARIA Singles Chart">ARIA Singles Chart</a>. She has sold over eight million albums globally and won three <a href="/wiki/World_Music_Awards" title="World Music Awards">World Music Awards</a>, 9 <a href="/wiki/ARIA_Music_Awards" title="ARIA Music Awards">ARIA Music Awards</a>, an <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award" title="MTV Video Music Award">MTV Video Music Award</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Delta_Goodrem" title="List of awards and nominations received by Delta Goodrem">several other awards</a>. From 2012 to 2013, she served as a coach on <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Voice_Australia" title="The Voice Australia">The Voice Australia</a></i>, and won <i><a href="/wiki/The_Voice_Kids_(Australian_TV_series)" title="The Voice Kids (Australian TV series)">The Voice Kids Australia</a></i> in 2014. She returned to <i>The Voice Australia</i> in 2015.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biography">Biography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delta_Goodrem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Biography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1984.E2.80.932000:_Early_life.2C_education.2C_and_discovery">1984–2000: Early life, education, and discovery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delta_Goodrem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1984–2000: Early life, education, and discovery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Goodrem was born on 9 November 1984,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bday_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-bday-1">[1]</a></sup> to Denis and Lea, who are now divorced. She has a younger brother, Trent,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> who is an <a href="/wiki/Australian_rules_football" title="Australian rules football">Australian rules football</a> player with the <a href="/wiki/Central_District_Football_Club" title="Central District Football Club">Central District Football Club</a> in the <a href="/wiki/South_Australian_National_Football_League" title="South Australian National Football League">South Australian National Football League</a> (SANFL).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Goodrem's parents named her Delta after <a href="/wiki/Joe_Cocker" title="Joe Cocker">Joe Cocker</a>'s song "Delta Lady".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> At the age of seven, Goodrem appeared in an American advertisement for the <a href="/wiki/Galoob" title="Galoob">Galoob</a> toy company, starring alongside fellow Australian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bec_Cartwright" title="Bec Cartwright">Bec Cartwright</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> and began playing piano at the same age while taking up singing, dancing and acting lessons. She appeared in numerous commercials for companies such as <a href="/wiki/Optus" title="Optus">Optus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nesquik" title="Nesquik">Nesquik</a>, and had several minor roles in episodes of successful Australian television shows including <i><a href="/wiki/Hey_Dad..!" title="Hey Dad..!">Hey Dad..!</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Country_Practice" title="A Country Practice">A Country Practice</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Police_Rescue" title="Police Rescue">Police Rescue</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>While residing at <a href="/wiki/Glenhaven,_New_South_Wales" title="Glenhaven, New South Wales">Glenhaven</a>, a suburb of Sydney, Goodrem attended <a href="/wiki/The_Hills_Grammar_School" title="The Hills Grammar School">the Hills Grammar School</a> in neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Kenthurst,_New_South_Wales" title="Kenthurst, New South Wales">Kenthurst</a>, from kindergarten until Year 10. She is known to return to her alma mater for visits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the age of thirteen, Goodrem recorded a five-song demo CD, financed through her television work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> It was sent to the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Swans" title="Sydney Swans">Sydney Swans</a> (of which Goodrem is a supporter) and they passed it onto <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Wheatley" title="Glenn Wheatley">Glenn Wheatley</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> the manager behind successful Australian artists, <a href="/wiki/Little_River_Band" title="Little River Band">Little River Band</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Farnham" title="John Farnham">John Farnham</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Storm_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Storm-10">[10]</a></sup> Interested in Goodrem's potential as a recording artist, Wheatley signed Goodrem to an <a href="/wiki/Artist_development_deal" title="Artist development deal">artist development deal</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independent_label" title="Independent label">independent label</a>, Empire Records.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Legal_quickstep_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Legal_quickstep-11">[11]</a></sup> Between June 1999 to September 2000, she worked with producers Paul Higgins and Trevor Carter on thirteen tracks for an album called <i><a href="/wiki/Delta_Goodrem_unreleased_tapes_dispute" title="Delta Goodrem unreleased tapes dispute">Delta</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Storm_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Storm-10">[10]</a></sup> which saw "an ambitious 15-year-old keen to emulate the pop sound of the <a href="/wiki/Spice_Girls" title="Spice Girls">Spice Girls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mandy_Moore" title="Mandy Moore">Mandy Moore</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The album has yet to surface, Goodrem preventing its release years later via <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_action" title="Civil action">civil action</a> in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Legal_quickstep_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Legal_quickstep-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2001.E2.80.9303:_Career_launch.2C_Neighbours.2C_Innocent_Eyes_and_cancer_diagnosis">2001–03: Career launch, <i>Neighbours</i>, <i>Innocent Eyes</i> and cancer diagnosis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delta_Goodrem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2001–03: Career launch, Neighbours, Innocent Eyes and cancer diagnosis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Verypretty_final.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="575" data-file-width="277" height="415" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Verypretty_final.jpg/200px-Verypretty_final.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f1/Verypretty_final.jpg 1.5x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Verypretty_final.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Goodrem at <a href="/wiki/The_Palazzo" title="The Palazzo">The Palazzo</a> resort in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<table class="mbox-small" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">

an impact on the charts.</div>

<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>At the age of 15, Goodrem signed a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Record_deal" title="Record deal">record deal</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sony_Music_Entertainment" title="Sony Music Entertainment">Sony</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-13">[13]</a></sup> and began work on an album of <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a>–<a href="/wiki/Dance_music" title="Dance music">dance</a> songs including the unsuccessful debut single, "<a href="/wiki/I_Don%27t_Care_(Angela_Via_song)" title="I Don't Care (Angela Via song)">I Don't Care</a>", which peaked at number sixty four on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ARIA_Singles_Chart" title="ARIA Singles Chart">ARIA Singles Chart</a> in November 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Storm_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-Storm-10">[10]</a></sup> The album and proposed second single "A Year Ago Today" were pushed aside as a result, allowing Goodrem and Sony to re-evaluate her future musical direction. In 2002, Goodrem took up the role as shy school girl and aspiring singer <a href="/wiki/Nina_Tucker" title="Nina Tucker">Nina Tucker</a> in the popular soap <i><a href="/wiki/Neighbours" title="Neighbours">Neighbours</a></i>, which helped re-launch Goodrem's music career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elevation_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Elevation-14">[14]</a></sup> The piano-based <a href="/wiki/Ballad" title="Ballad">ballad</a> "<a href="/wiki/Born_to_Try" title="Born to Try">Born to Try</a>", co-written by <a href="/wiki/Audius_Mtawarira" title="Audius Mtawarira">Audius Mtawarira</a>, premiered on the show and reached number one on the ARIA Singles Chart and number three in the UK. Born to Try was certified triple Platinum in Australia for sales of over 210,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2003_Singles_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-2003_Singles-15">[15]</a></sup> Goodrem's role on the show scored her a <a href="/wiki/Logie_Awards" title="Logie Awards">Logie</a> for "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Logie_Award_for_Most_Popular_New_Talent" title="Logie Award for Most Popular New Talent">Most Popular New Talent</a>" at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2003_Logie_Awards" title="2003 Logie Awards">2003 Logie Awards</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> In January 2003, "<a href="/wiki/Lost_Without_You" title="Lost Without You">Lost Without You</a>" topped the ARIA Singles Chart and reached number four in the UK. it was certified double platinum for sales over 140,000 copies in Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2003_Singles_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-2003_Singles-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Goodrem's largely self-penned debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Innocent_Eyes_(Delta_Goodrem_album)" title="Innocent Eyes (Delta Goodrem album)">Innocent Eyes</a></i>, was released on 21 March 2003 in Australia and debuted at number one on the ARIA Album Charts, breaking Australian records previously held by <a href="/wiki/John_Farnham" title="John Farnham">John Farnham</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Whispering_Jack" title="Whispering Jack">Whispering Jack</a></i> (1986) by staying at number one for 25 consecutive weeks, while tying with <a href="/wiki/Neil_Diamond" title="Neil Diamond">Neil Diamond</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Hot_August_Night" title="Hot August Night">Hot August Night</a></i> (1972) as the second longest charting number one album with a total of 29 weeks at top spot. It was the highest-selling album in Australia of 2003<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adams_2003_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Adams_2003-17">[17]</a></sup> and sold 1.2 million copies in Australia, and over 4 million worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The album also charted highly in the UK, peaking at number two. The album's third single "<a href="/wiki/Innocent_Eyes_(song)" title="Innocent Eyes (song)">Innocent Eyes</a>" again reached number one on the ARIA Singles Chart and number nine in the UK. it was certified Platinum in Australia for sales over 70,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2003_Singles_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-2003_Singles-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 8 July 2003, at the age of 18, Goodrem was diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Hodgkin%27s_lymphoma" title="Hodgkin's lymphoma">Hodgkin's lymphoma</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> She was forced to put all working commitments on hold while undertaking treatment for the disease. In an exclusive interview with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Australian_Women%27s_Weekly" title="The Australian Women's Weekly">The Australian Women's Weekly</a></i>, Goodrem revealed that, since 2002, she had suffered from a head-to-toe rash, fatigue, weight loss, night sweats, and a lump on her neck.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-darkesthour_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-darkesthour-20">[20]</a></sup> "I was doing sit-ups when I felt something pop in my neck. I reached down and I felt a small lump at the base of my throat. It wasn't sore, it wasn't visible, but I could feel it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-darkesthour_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-darkesthour-20">[20]</a></sup> As part of her treatment, Goodrem undertook <a href="/wiki/Chemotherapy" title="Chemotherapy">chemotherapy</a>, which resulted in the loss of her hair, and <a href="/wiki/Radiation_therapy" title="Radiation therapy">radiation therapy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-darkesthour_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-darkesthour-20">[20]</a></sup> The news of her diagnosis made newspaper and television headlines and an outpouring of support was shown by fans and the general public alike. Goodrem thanked them during <a href="/wiki/The_Visualise_Tour" title="The Visualise Tour">The Visualise Tour</a> for all the letters and well wishes she received.</p>
<p>The album's fourth single, "<a href="/wiki/Not_Me,_Not_I" title="Not Me, Not I">Not Me, Not I</a>", was released following the announcement Goodrem had been diagnosed with cancer. It became her fourth consecutive number one single in Australia, overtaking the previous effort of three number-ones from <a href="/wiki/Kylie_Minogue" title="Kylie Minogue">Kylie Minogue</a>'s debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Kylie_(album)" title="Kylie (album)">Kylie</a></i> (1988).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> It was certified Platinum for sales over 70,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2003_Singles_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-2003_Singles-15">[15]</a></sup> In early August, Goodrem announced she would not renew her contract with <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Wheatley" title="Glenn Wheatley">Glenn Wheatley</a>. Her mother, Lea Goodrem, replaced him as her manager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Later that month, Goodrem won seven <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ARIA_Awards" title="ARIA Awards">ARIA Awards</a>, including "Best Female Artist", surpassing <a href="/wiki/Natalie_Imbruglia" title="Natalie Imbruglia">Natalie Imbruglia</a>'s previous record of six awards in 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> As Delta was too unwell to perform at the ceremony herself, singer <a href="/wiki/Darren_Hayes" title="Darren Hayes">Darren Hayes</a> performed a rendition of "Lost Without You" as a tribute, bringing an overwhelmed Goodrem to tears. Her first full-length DVD <i><a href="/wiki/Delta_(video_album)" title="Delta (video album)">Delta</a></i> became the highest-selling music DVD by an Australian artist in Australia ever, with a certification of 11x platinum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The Australian-only release "<a href="/wiki/Predictable_(Delta_Goodrem_song)" title="Predictable (Delta Goodrem song)">Predictable</a>" became her fifth consecutive number one on the ARIA Singles Chart in December and was certified double Platinum for sales of over 140,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2003_Singles_15-4"><a href="#cite_note-2003_Singles-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2004.E2.80.9306:_Mistaken_Identity_and_The_Visualise_Tour">2004–06: <i>Mistaken Identity</i> and The Visualise Tour</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delta_Goodrem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2004–06: Mistaken Identity and The Visualise Tour">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After announcing in late December 2003 that she was in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Remission_(medicine)" title="Remission (medicine)">remission</a>, Goodrem began work on her second studio album. Goodrem received two nominations at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_Logie_Awards" title="2004 Logie Awards">2004 Logie Awards</a> including a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gold_Logie_Award_for_Most_Popular_Personality_on_Australian_Television" title="Gold Logie Award for Most Popular Personality on Australian Television">Gold Logie</a> nomination for "Most Popular Personality on Australian Television". In September 2004, she became the face of soft drink company <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a> in Australia, appearing on the product, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Billboards" title="Billboards">billboards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Television_advertisement" title="Television advertisement">TV advertisements</a> and performing an exclusive show for competition winners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> In October Goodrem launched her own lingerie line titled "Delta by Annabella".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Delta_Goodrem_in_Concert_Cropped.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="666" data-file-width="551" height="242" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Delta_Goodrem_in_Concert_Cropped.jpg/200px-Delta_Goodrem_in_Concert_Cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Delta_Goodrem_in_Concert_Cropped.jpg/300px-Delta_Goodrem_in_Concert_Cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Delta_Goodrem_in_Concert_Cropped.jpg/400px-Delta_Goodrem_in_Concert_Cropped.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Delta_Goodrem_in_Concert_Cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Delta Goodrem in concert</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Goodrem's second album <i><a href="/wiki/Mistaken_Identity_(Delta_Goodrem_album)" title="Mistaken Identity (Delta Goodrem album)">Mistaken Identity</a></i>, was released in Australia on 8 November 2004 and debuted at number one on the ARIA Albums chart. It was certified five times platinum for sales of 350,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The album spent 46 weeks in the top fifty. It also reached number seven in New Zealand, and peaked at number 25 in the UK. The album's lead single "<a href="/wiki/Out_of_the_Blue_(Delta_Goodrem_song)" title="Out of the Blue (Delta Goodrem song)">Out of the Blue</a>", which was co-written and produced by <a href="/wiki/Guy_Chambers" title="Guy Chambers">Guy Chambers</a> was released prior to the album on 8 October 2004. "Out of the Blue" debuted at number one on the ARIA Singles Chart and number nine in the UK". This was Goodrem's sixth straight number one single in Australia. It was certified platinum in Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> The second single "<a href="/wiki/Mistaken_Identity_(Delta_Goodrem_song)" title="Mistaken Identity (Delta Goodrem song)">Mistaken Identity</a>" was released only in Australia debuted at number seven and was certified Gold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARIA2005_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-ARIA2005-30">[30]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Almost_Here_(Brian_McFadden_and_Delta_Goodrem_song)" title="Almost Here (Brian McFadden and Delta Goodrem song)">Almost Here</a>", a duet with Irish singer <a href="/wiki/Brian_McFadden" title="Brian McFadden">Brian McFadden</a> was released as the third single and reached number three in the UK and became her seventh ARIA number one, along with her first number one in Ireland. It was certified platinum in Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARIA2005_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-ARIA2005-30">[30]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/A_Little_Too_Late_(Delta_Goodrem_song)" title="A Little Too Late (Delta Goodrem song)">A Little Too Late</a>" was released only in Australia and peaked at number 13. "<a href="/wiki/Be_Strong" title="Be Strong">Be Strong</a>" was released as the album's fifth and final single in Australia as a <a href="/wiki/Music_download" title="Music download">digital download</a> on 16 October 2005. At the time of release, digital downloads were not included as part of the main singles chart, therefore it was ineligible to chart. Much of the album, in particular "Extraordinary Day", was inspired by her battle with cancer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-31">[31]</a></sup> Reflecting on that period of her life, Goodrem said "It's weird to see pictures of that time. In some ways the fact that I was so sick was so out there, and yet I kept it really private. No-one saw me on the days I was really sick. I was 18 when I was diagnosed and I had a number one album and single in the country. And in the UK, I was number two. It was such a bipolar year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<table class="mbox-small" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;">
<tr>

<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing these files? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>

<p>In March 2005, Goodrem starred in her first film role in <i><a href="/wiki/Hating_Alison_Ashley_(film)" title="Hating Alison Ashley (film)">Hating Alison Ashley</a></i>, a film based on the <a href="/wiki/Hating_Alison_Ashley_(novel)" title="Hating Alison Ashley (novel)">children's novel</a> by <a href="/wiki/Robin_Klein" title="Robin Klein">Robin Klein</a>, with Goodrem acting the title character. The film performed poorly at the box office and was not a critical success, with some critics citing Goodrem's performance as too robotic and detached.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> April 2005 saw Goodrem relocate to New York to launch her career in the United States with a re-worked version of "<a href="/wiki/Lost_Without_You" title="Lost Without You">Lost Without You</a>". She appeared in the last two episodes of the short-lived American series <i><a href="/wiki/North_Shore_(TV_series)" title="North Shore (TV series)">North Shore</a></i> in a bid to gain greater exposure. "Lost Without You" proved to be modestly successful, peaking at number eighteen on the <a href="/wiki/Adult_Contemporary_(chart)" title="Adult Contemporary (chart)">Billboard Adult Contemporary chart</a>, but Goodrem was reportedly dissatisfied with its performance. Plans to release a hybrid of her first two albums were later terminated and Goodrem put America on hold. In July, Goodrem embarked on her first headline <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Concert_tour" title="Concert tour">concert tour</a> of Australia, <a href="/wiki/The_Visualise_Tour" title="The Visualise Tour">The Visualise Tour</a>. Ticket prices, $90 each, came under criticism for being higher than most international acts touring Australia at the time and this initially led to slow sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> By the time the concerts were due to take place, many venues sold out after tickets were reduced to $60. Once the tour concluded, over 80,000 tickets had been bought in total making The Visualise Tour one of Australia's highest-selling local tours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Visualise_Tour:_Live_in_Concert" title="The Visualise Tour: Live in Concert">The Visualise Tour: Live in Concert</a></i> was released in November and became Goodrem's second No. 1 DVD.</p>
<p>On 15 March 2006, Goodrem performed a new song, "<a href="/wiki/Together_We_Are_One" title="Together We Are One">Together We Are One</a>", at the <a href="/wiki/2006_Commonwealth_Games_opening_ceremony" title="2006 Commonwealth Games opening ceremony">Commonwealth Games opening ceremony</a> in front of 80,000 spectators and up to 1.5 billion television viewers worldwide. The song, written specifically for the event was released in Australia where it peaked at number two on the ARIA Singles Chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> It was performed by the Top 5 contestants on <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_5)" title="American Idol (season 5)">season five</a> of "<a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a>". In June 2006, Goodrem signed to Modest! Entertainment for her worldwide management.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> In October 2006, Goodrem promoted in Japan with the release of an updated version of <i><a href="/wiki/Innocent_Eyes_(Delta_Goodrem_album)" title="Innocent Eyes (Delta Goodrem album)">Innocent Eyes</a></i> and the Japan-only single "<a href="/wiki/Flawed_(song)" title="Flawed (song)">Flawed</a>", which reached number one on the Japanese download chart. The album peaked at number eight on the Japanese international chart (excluding Japanese artists) and number nineteen on the official Japanese album chart (including Japanese artists). In November, Goodrem appeared with <a href="/wiki/Westlife" title="Westlife">Westlife</a> on UK talent series <i><a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK_series_3)" title="The X Factor (UK series 3)">The X Factor</a></i> to perform a duet titled "<a href="/wiki/All_Out_of_Love" title="All Out of Love">All Out of Love</a>", which appeared on the boyband's ninth LP, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Love_Album_(Westlife_album)" title="The Love Album (Westlife album)">The Love Album</a></i>. She was in Melbourne on Christmas Eve to headline the annual <a href="/wiki/Carols_by_Candlelight" title="Carols by Candlelight">Carols by Candlelight</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2007.E2.80.9310:_Delta_and_Believe_Again_Tour">2007–10: <i>Delta</i> and Believe Again Tour</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delta_Goodrem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2007–10: Delta and Believe Again Tour">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Goodrem's third studio album, the eponymous <i><a href="/wiki/Delta_(Delta_Goodrem_album)" title="Delta (Delta Goodrem album)">Delta</a></i>, was released in Australia on 20 October 2007. Goodrem described the material as "...a lot lighter" compared to her previous album <i>Mistaken Identity</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> She has also stated, "As people become more aware of your life, they can pinpoint what songs are about. On this album, I've tried to remove a lot of that and just write great pop songs, songs that are from my heart but there's no baggage with them".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The album debuted at number one on the ARIA Albums Chart, making it her third number one album in her home country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elevation_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Elevation-14">[14]</a></sup> and received <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Platinum_record" title="Platinum record">platinum</a> certification for shipments of 70,000 records, though sales were much lower; only 23,000 copies were sold during the first week. In December the album was certified 2x platinum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> It eventually was certified 3x platinum in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In New Zealand, the album debuted at number twelve on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RIANZ_Albums_Chart" title="RIANZ Albums Chart">RIANZ Albums Chart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 10 August 2007, Goodrem was in Los Angeles to film the music video for the album's lead single "<a href="/wiki/In_This_Life_(Delta_Goodrem_song)" title="In This Life (Delta Goodrem song)">In This Life</a>", which is also the opening theme for the anime <i><a href="/wiki/Deltora_Quest_(anime)" title="Deltora Quest (anime)">Deltora Quest</a></i>, based on the <a href="/wiki/Deltora_Quest_(series)" title="Deltora Quest (series)">novels</a> by fellow Australian <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Rowe" title="Jennifer Rowe">Emily Rodda</a>. The video premiered on 31 August on <i><a href="/wiki/Sunrise_(TV_program)" title="Sunrise (TV program)">Sunrise</a></i>. "In This Life" was officially released on 15 September. It debuted at number one on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_Singles_Chart" title="Australian Singles Chart">Australian Singles Chart</a>, becoming Goodrem's eighth number one single in Australia. It was certified platinum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Delta_Goodrem_Melbourne_13.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Delta_Goodrem_Melbourne_13.jpg/180px-Delta_Goodrem_Melbourne_13.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Delta_Goodrem_Melbourne_13.jpg/270px-Delta_Goodrem_Melbourne_13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Delta_Goodrem_Melbourne_13.jpg/360px-Delta_Goodrem_Melbourne_13.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Delta_Goodrem_Melbourne_13.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Goodrem performing during promotion in Australia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The second single, "<a href="/wiki/Believe_Again" title="Believe Again">Believe Again</a>" was released on 10 December. It debuted and peaked at number two on the ARIA Singles Chart and was certified Gold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The third single, "<a href="/wiki/You_Will_Only_Break_My_Heart" title="You Will Only Break My Heart">You Will Only Break My Heart</a>", was released on 29 March 2008 and peaked at number fourteen. The fourth single to be lifted from the album was "<a href="/wiki/I_Can%27t_Break_It_to_My_Heart" title="I Can't Break It to My Heart">I Can't Break It to My Heart</a>", which debuted and peaked at number thirteen. Following the release of the lead single, Goodrem currently holds the record for most number one singles on the ARIA charts by any artist, with a total of 8.</p>
<p>In 2008, Goodrem focused on promoting music in Japan and the United States. She released "In This Life" on 23 January in Japan. She followed that up by releasing "Delta" on 20 February. The album peaked at number eight on the Japanese international chart and number 39 on the overall chart. The album sold almost 5,000 copies in its first week, 1,000 copies more than her previous album in Japan and overall sold over 30,000 copies in Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InterJap_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-InterJap-48">[48]</a></sup> In the United States, Goodrem released "In This Life" on 15 April 2008. "In This Life" was released to US radio on 9 April. It was first released to the Triple A radio format, and then to the Adult Contemporary and Hot Adult Contemporary formats. On 17 June 2008, Goodrem appeared for the second time on any <i>Billboard</i> chart with the single, debuting at number 40 on the <a href="/wiki/Adult_Top_40" title="Adult Top 40">Hot Adult Top 40 Tracks</a> chart. The song later peaked at No. 21.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a>, the track sold 7,000 digital downloads in the week ending on 24 June 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The song also charted at number 20 on the Hot Adult Top 40 Recurrents. The album was then released on 15 July 2008 in the United States and Canada under the label <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Records" title="Mercury Records">Mercury Records</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USReleasedate_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-USReleasedate-51">[51]</a></sup> It peaked at number 18 on the U.S. <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Store</a>. It later debuted at number 116 on the US Billboard Album Chart and No. 1 on Billboard's Top Heatseekers with sales of 6,000 copies. Overall the album sold over 21,000 copies in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Debute_sales_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Debute_sales-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goodrem_tops_Top_Heatseekers_Chart_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Goodrem_tops_Top_Heatseekers_Chart-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2008, it was announced that Goodrem would embark on a national tour of Australia, titled the <a href="/wiki/Believe_Again_Tour" title="Believe Again Tour">Believe Again Tour</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> She originally announced nine dates in seven cities, but later announced more shows, performing 14 in eight cities. The tour ran from 9 January to 4 February 2009. A concert DVD of the tour was released on 18 September 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> It was called <a href="/wiki/Believe_Again:_Australian_Tour_2009" title="Believe Again: Australian Tour 2009">Believe Again: Australian Tour 2009</a>. It peaked at number one on the Australian <a href="/wiki/ARIA_Charts" title="ARIA Charts">ARIA</a> DVD Chart and was certified Gold for sales over 7,500 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>Goodrem also recorded a duet, "Right Here With You", with <a href="/wiki/Olivia_Newton-John" title="Olivia Newton-John">Olivia Newton-John</a> to help raise money for Newton-John's cancer hospital in Melbourne.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<table class="mbox-small" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;">
<tr>

<div class="center">

<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>

</table>
<p>Goodrem was nominated for two awards at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008_ARIA_Awards" title="2008 ARIA Awards">2008 ARIA Awards</a> – Highest Selling Single and Highest Selling Album – and won the award for Highest Selling Album of 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goodrem_to_tour_in_New_Year_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Goodrem_to_tour_in_New_Year-59">[59]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2008_World_Music_Awards" title="2008 World Music Awards">2008 World Music Awards</a>, held on 9 November in Monaco, Goodrem received her third <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Music_Award" title="World Music Award">World Music Award</a> for World's Best Selling Australian Artist. In March 2010, Goodrem and <a href="/wiki/Guy_Sebastian" title="Guy Sebastian">Guy Sebastian</a> were chosen by the Jackson estate to perform at the Australian launch of <i><a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson%27s_This_Is_It" title="Michael Jackson's This Is It">Michael Jackson's This Is It</a></i> DVD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The invitation-only event was attended by the film's director <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Ortega" title="Kenny Ortega">Kenny Ortega</a>, Jackson's choreographer <a href="/wiki/Travis_Payne" title="Travis Payne">Travis Payne</a>, and Jackson's brother <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Jackson" title="Jackie Jackson">Jackie Jackson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Goodrem and Sebastian performed "<a href="/wiki/Earth_Song" title="Earth Song">Earth Song</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011.E2.80.9314:_Child_of_the_Universe.2C_The_Voice">2011–14: <i>Child of the Universe</i>, <i>The Voice</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delta_Goodrem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2011–14: Child of the Universe, The Voice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Delta_Goodrem2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1625" data-file-width="1047" height="279" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Delta_Goodrem2012.jpg/180px-Delta_Goodrem2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Delta_Goodrem2012.jpg/270px-Delta_Goodrem2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Delta_Goodrem2012.jpg/360px-Delta_Goodrem2012.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Delta_Goodrem2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Goodrem at the 2012 Logie Awards</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 24 November 2011, Goodrem was confirmed to be a part of the judging panel of the <a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(Australian_TV_series)" title="The Voice (Australian TV series)">Australian version</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(TV_series)" title="The Voice (TV series)">The Voice</a></i> which aired in early 2012, coaching alongside <a href="/wiki/Keith_Urban" title="Keith Urban">Keith Urban</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joel_Madden" title="Joel Madden">Joel Madden</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Seal_(musician)" title="Seal (musician)">Seal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Some of Goodrem's decisions on the show sparked criticism, with comments she was "all style" and "little substance".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rachael_Leahcar" title="Rachael Leahcar">Rachael Leahcar</a> was Goodrem's contestant in the final four. This was after Goodrem chose Leahcar over Glenn Cunningham, who was Goodrem's back up singer on her <a href="/wiki/Believe_Again_Tour" title="Believe Again Tour">Believe Again Tour</a> in 2009. Leahcar finished third. Goodrem returned for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Voice_(Australia_series_2)" title="The Voice (Australia series 2)">season two</a> in 2013, again with Madden and Seal, with <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Martin" title="Ricky Martin">Ricky Martin</a> replacing Urban. Goodrem's finalist for season two was Celia Pavey who also finished third.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>An announcement was made on 19 March 2012, stating that there is now a countdown on Goodrem's official website to 30 March, with the promise of "something new, something fresh, something altogether exciting". On that day, it was then announced that Goodrem would be releasing her new single, "<a href="/wiki/Sitting_on_Top_of_the_World_(Delta_Goodrem_song)" title="Sitting on Top of the World (Delta Goodrem song)">Sitting on Top of the World</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> "Sitting on Top of the World" debuted and peaked at number two on the ARIA Singles Chart and was certified double platinum. It also peaked number twenty three in New Zealand and was certified Gold. The album's second single, "<a href="/wiki/Dancing_with_a_Broken_Heart" title="Dancing with a Broken Heart">Dancing with a Broken Heart</a>" was released on 10 August 2012. It debuted and peaked at number 15 on the ARIA Singles Chart, and is Goodrem's second lowest charting single to date. The third single, "<a href="/wiki/Wish_You_Were_Here_(Delta_Goodrem_song)" title="Wish You Were Here (Delta Goodrem song)">Wish You Were Here</a>", was released on 12 October 2012. "Wish You Were Here" debuted at number seven on the ARIA Charts and later peaked at number five, and was certified Platinum. Goodrem's fourth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Child_of_the_Universe_(album)" title="Child of the Universe (album)">Child of the Universe</a></i> was released on 26 October 2012, which debuted at number two on the ARIA Charts and spent ten weeks in the top 50. It was certified Gold in its second with for sales of 35,000 copies. Along with the release of the album, Goodrem embarked on her "<a href="/wiki/An_Evening_with_Delta:_The_Top_of_My_World_Shows" title="An Evening with Delta: The Top of My World Shows">An Evening with Delta: The Top of My World Shows</a>" which supported the album release with a series of stripped back shows, starting in Brisbane on 27 October then two Sydney shows on 31 October 2012 and 2 November 2012 and finishing with Melbourne on 7 and 8 November 2012. <a href="/wiki/Rachael_Leahcar" title="Rachael Leahcar">Rachael Leahcar</a> was the tour's opening act.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Goodrem was featured on the album "Spirit of Christmas 2012", singing "Blue Christmas". In November, she also recorded a Christmas EP titled <i><a href="/wiki/Christmas_(Delta_Goodrem_EP)" title="Christmas (Delta Goodrem EP)">Christmas</a></i>. It was released on 14 December 2012 in Australia and New Zealand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 1 February 2013, it was confirmed that Goodrem had signed with US manager <a href="/wiki/Irving_Azoff" title="Irving Azoff">Irving Azoff</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Goodrem performed at the Mardi Gras in Sydney in March 2013. This was a late night performance, in Mardigrasland, which was well received by critics. She performed dance version of some of her hit songs including "<a href="/wiki/Born_to_Try" title="Born to Try">Born to Try</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Lost_Without_You" title="Lost Without You">Lost Without You</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Predictable_(Delta_Goodrem_song)" title="Predictable (Delta Goodrem song)">Predictable</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Believe_Again" title="Believe Again">Believe Again</a>", "Child of the Universe" and "<a href="/wiki/Sitting_on_Top_of_the_World_(Delta_Goodrem_song)" title="Sitting on Top of the World (Delta Goodrem song)">Sitting on Top of the World</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> In May 2013, <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Gurrumul_Yunupingu" title="Geoffrey Gurrumul Yunupingu">Geoffrey Gurrumul Yunupingu</a> joined Goodrem for a special performance of "Bayini" on <i>The Voice Australia</i>, in celebration of National Reconciliation Week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The song was later released on iTunes and debuted at number four on the ARIA Singles Chart on 10 June 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> On 17 June 2013, Goodrem released her new single "<a href="/wiki/Heart_Hypnotic" title="Heart Hypnotic">Heart Hypnotic</a>", which she also premiered on the Live Finale of <i>The Voice</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thevoice_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-thevoice-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>Goodrem celebrated 10 years since releasing her multi-platinum album <i><a href="/wiki/Innocent_Eyes_(Delta_Goodrem_album)" title="Innocent Eyes (Delta Goodrem album)">Innocent Eyes</a></i> which topped the Australian ARIA Charts and reached number two on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a> by releasing <i><a href="/wiki/Innocent_Eyes:_Ten_Year_Anniversary_Acoustic_Edition" title="Innocent Eyes: Ten Year Anniversary Acoustic Edition">Innocent Eyes: Ten Year Anniversary Acoustic Edition</a></i> on 29 November 2013, which debuted and peaked at number 22 on the ARIA Albums Chart.On 26 November 2013, it was announced that Goodrem would not be returning to <i>The Voice Australia</i> for a third season but instead chose to be a part of the new Australian version of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Voice_Kids_(Australian_TV_series)" title="The Voice Kids (Australian TV series)">The Voice Kids</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Goodrem revealed on her <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> account that the decision was made because this would give her more time on her music career and more time to work on her new album. The show premiered on 22 June 2014 and finished on 10 August .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Goodrem was a coach alongside <a href="/wiki/Joel_Madden" title="Joel Madden">Joel Madden</a>, who teamed up with his brother <a href="/wiki/Benji_Madden" title="Benji Madden">Benji Madden</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mel_B" title="Mel B">Mel B</a>. <a href="/wiki/Darren_McMullen" title="Darren McMullen">Darren McMullen</a> hosted <i>The Voice Kids</i> while also remaining on the original version.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Goodrem attended the <a href="/wiki/3rd_AACTA_Awards" title="3rd AACTA Awards">2014 AACTA Awards</a> where she performed "<a href="/wiki/Kissing_You_(Des%27ree_song)" title="Kissing You (Des'ree song)">Kissing You</a>" in tribute to <a href="/wiki/Baz_Luhrmann" title="Baz Luhrmann">Baz Luhrmann</a>'s film <i><a href="/wiki/Romeo_%2B_Juliet" title="Romeo + Juliet">Romeo + Juliet</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Goodrem joined the Australian and New Zealand leg of <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Bocelli" title="Andrea Bocelli">Andrea Bocelli</a>'s Passion For Life Tour in September 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> To celebrate being part of the tour, Goodrem released a cover of <a href="/wiki/Martika" title="Martika">Martika</a>'s 1991 single "<a href="/wiki/Love..._Thy_Will_Be_Done#Delta_Goodrem_version" title="Love... Thy Will Be Done">Love... Thy Will Be Done</a>" on 12 September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015.E2.80.93present:_Return_to_Neighbours.2C_stage_debut_and_Wings_of_the_Wild">2015–present: Return to <i>Neighbours</i>, stage debut and <i>Wings of the Wild</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delta_Goodrem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2015–present: Return to Neighbours, stage debut and Wings of the Wild">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>It was announced on 13 January 2015, that Goodrem would return to her judging chair on <i>The Voice Australia</i> for the series' fourth season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Goodrem's single "<a href="/wiki/Only_Human_(Delta_Goodrem_song)" title="Only Human (Delta Goodrem song)">Only Human</a>" was released on 13 March to coincide with her return as <a href="/wiki/Nina_Tucker" title="Nina Tucker">Nina Tucker</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/Neighbours" title="Neighbours">Neighbours</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span> 30th anniversary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martin_Tour_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Martin_Tour-86">[86]</a></sup> She returned for three episodes starting from 16 March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Goodrem also appeared in a documentary special celebrating the anniversary titled <i>Neighbours 30th: The Stars Reunite</i>, which aired in Australia and the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> She joined the Australian leg of Ricky Martin's One World Tour in April as his supporting act.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martin_Tour_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-Martin_Tour-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> She also revealed that she has been working with <a href="/wiki/DNA_Songs" title="DNA Songs">DNA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jon_Hume" title="Jon Hume">Jon Hume</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Wings_(Delta_Goodrem_song)" title="Wings (Delta Goodrem song)">Wings</a>" was released as the lead single from her fifth studio album on 24 July 2015. The song peaked at number one on the ARIA Charts and was certified Platinum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Goodrem also promoted the single in New Zealand and the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> From October 2015 to February 2016, Goodrem made her musical theatre debut playing <a href="/wiki/Grizabella" title="Grizabella">Grizabella</a> in an Australian version of <a href="/wiki/Cats_(musical)" title="Cats (musical)">Cats</a>. She performed the role in the Sydney, Hobart, Melbourne and Brisbane legs of the show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Dear_Life_(song)" title="Dear Life (song)">Dear Life</a>" was released on 6 May 2016 as the second single from <i>Wings of the Wild</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The single debuted and peaked at number three on the ARIA Singles Chart and was later certified Gold. "<a href="/wiki/Enough_(Delta_Goodrem_song)" title="Enough (Delta Goodrem song)">Enough</a>" featuring rapper Gizzle was released as the third single on 24 June 2016 and debuted at number forty six on the ARIA Singles Chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Wings_of_the_Wild" title="Wings of the Wild">Wings of the Wild</a></i> was released on 1 July 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-News.com.au_1_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-News.com.au_1-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mix1049.com.au_1_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mix1049.com.au_1-104">[104]</a></sup> The River was later released with an story music video for the tour in September 2016, while she was in New Zealand. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Delta is scheduled to make her House Husbands debut in 2017 <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delta_Goodrem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2004, Goodrem began a nine-month relationship with Australian tennis player <a href="/wiki/Mark_Philippoussis" title="Mark Philippoussis">Mark Philippoussis</a>. Her "comeback" single, "<a href="/wiki/Out_of_the_Blue_(Delta_Goodrem_song)" title="Out of the Blue (Delta Goodrem song)">Out of the Blue</a>", was written about his support during her cancer battle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> The couple's relationship ended in controversy when newspapers reported Philippoussis had been unfaithful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>Later in 2004, Goodrem began dating former <a href="/wiki/Westlife" title="Westlife">Westlife</a> singer <a href="/wiki/Brian_McFadden" title="Brian McFadden">Brian McFadden</a> with whom she collaborated on the duet "Almost Here". The pair ended their relationship in April 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> In May 2011, Goodrem started dating <a href="/wiki/Nick_Jonas" title="Nick Jonas">Nick Jonas</a>. They broke up in February 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy_and_artistry">Legacy and artistry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delta_Goodrem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Legacy and artistry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Delta_wax_at_Madame_Tussauds_Sydney.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1000" height="270" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Delta_wax_at_Madame_Tussauds_Sydney.jpg/180px-Delta_wax_at_Madame_Tussauds_Sydney.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Delta_wax_at_Madame_Tussauds_Sydney.jpg/270px-Delta_wax_at_Madame_Tussauds_Sydney.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Delta_wax_at_Madame_Tussauds_Sydney.jpg/360px-Delta_wax_at_Madame_Tussauds_Sydney.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Delta_wax_at_Madame_Tussauds_Sydney.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A wax figure of Goodrem at <a href="/wiki/Madame_Tussauds" title="Madame Tussauds">Madame Tussauds</a> Sydney</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Goodrem's repertoire falls under the <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adult_contemporary_music" title="Adult contemporary music">adult contemporary</a> styles, and heavily features the piano, which she usually plays barefoot while performing live.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Goodrem is also known for her technically skilled <a href="/wiki/Soprano" title="Soprano">soprano</a> voice,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> which in a review of <i>Delta</i> was described as crystalline, fierce and illuminating in quality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Delta has also endorsed many things such as WII, Sanitarium, So Good, Nesquik, Sunsilk and Pepsi<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>Goodrem was honoured with a wax figure at <a href="/wiki/Madame_Tussauds" title="Madame Tussauds">Madame Tussauds</a> in Sydney's <a href="/wiki/Darling_Harbour" title="Darling Harbour">Darling Harbour</a>, which opened in April 2012. The singer donated to the attraction a dress that she had previously worn on stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>Her debut album, 2003's <i><a href="/wiki/Innocent_Eyes_(Delta_Goodrem_album)" title="Innocent Eyes (Delta Goodrem album)">Innocent Eyes</a></i>, made her one of Australia's highest-selling female recording artists, spending 29 weeks at No. 1,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adams_2003_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Adams_2003-17">[17]</a></sup> selling over 1.2 million copies in Australia and another 4.5 million internationally, debuting at number 2 in the UK and breaking various records in the process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2004, Goodrem released <i><a href="/wiki/Mistaken_Identity_(Delta_Goodrem_album)" title="Mistaken Identity (Delta Goodrem album)">Mistaken Identity</a></i>, her second studio album which entered the ARIA charts at No. 1 spawning two No. 1 singles and quickly gained multi-platinum status. In 2005, Goodrem embarked on <a href="/wiki/The_Visualise_Tour" title="The Visualise Tour">The Visualise Tour</a>, her debut <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Concert_tour" title="Concert tour">concert tour</a> of Australia, combining songs from both <i>Innocent Eyes</i> and <i>Mistaken Identity</i>. Goodrem released her third studio album, self-titled <i><a href="/wiki/Delta_(Delta_Goodrem_album)" title="Delta (Delta Goodrem album)">Delta</a></i>, on 20 October 2007 to yet another number-one debut, gaining multi-platinum status within the first few months of release. Goodrem also shifted attention to different markets, releasing the album in the Far East and the USA. In January 2009, Goodrem embarked on the <a href="/wiki/Believe_Again_Tour" title="Believe Again Tour">Believe Again Tour</a> of Australia to support her third studio album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goodrem_to_tour_in_New_Year_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-Goodrem_to_tour_in_New_Year-59">[59]</a></sup> Her fourth album <i>Child of the Universe</i> had two platinum singles, "Sitting On Top of the World" and "Wish You Were Here". Her fifth album, <i>Wings of the Wild</i> became her fourth No. 1 album on the ARIA Albums Chart, while producing the No. 1 single "Wings".</p>
<p>Goodrem has a total of nine number-one singles and 17 top-ten hits on the ARIA Singles Chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elevation_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-Elevation-14">[14]</a></sup> She has sold over eight million albums globally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delta_Goodrem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Philanthropy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In May 2005, Goodrem helped launch "Teen Info on Cancer", a UK website aimed at supporting young teenage sufferers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> In November 2005, Goodrem became an ambassador for Research Australia's "Thank You Day", which honours the country's health and medical researchers and received a Thank You Day Celebrity Advocacy Award "in recognition of her efforts in raising funds and awareness for Australian medical research and charities."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>Goodrem is set to be the face of Alternative Hair, the UK hairdressing industry's top fundraising event, in aid of cancer charity Leukaemia Research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Goodrem is also a member of RADD (Recording Artists, Actors And Athletes Against Drink Driving), a group of celebrities raising awareness of the risks of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drunk_driving" title="Drunk driving">drunk driving</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> In 2011 Goodrem became an ambassador for the Kinghorn Cancer Centre at Sydney's <a href="/wiki/Garvan_Institute_of_Medical_Research" title="Garvan Institute of Medical Research">Garvan Institute of Medical Research</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delta_Goodrem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Discography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_recognitions">Awards and recognitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Delta_Goodrem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Awards and recognitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Delta_Goodrem" title="List of awards and nominations received by Delta Goodrem">List of awards and nominations received by Delta Goodrem</a></div>
